                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:8px;border-left-width:7px;border-right-width:7px;border-color:white transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483647;top:30px;left:50%;margin-left:-7px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                </div>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:9px;border-left-width:8px;border-right-width:8px;border-color:#e7e7e7 transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483646;top:29px;left:50%;margin-left:-8px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                </div>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="position:absolute;overflow:hidden;margin-top:-3px;margin-left:-35px;top:40px;left:50%;right:;display:inline-block;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                 <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">
                  <div style="width:60px;height:20px;">
                   <iframe allowtransparency="true" frameborder="0" scrolling="no" src="//platform.twitter.com/widgets/follow_button.html?screen_name=YahooTravel&amp;show_screen_name=false&amp;show_count=false" style="border:none;overflow:hidden;width:60px;height:20px;">
                   </iframe>
                  </div>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="Pos-r D-ib Cur-d Va-t" style="height:40px;">
               <div class="D-ib" style="height:40px;padding:0 11.5px;">
                <a class="D-ib" href="https://www.instagram.com/yahootravel" rel="me" target="_blank">
                 <i class="Icon Fw-n Va-t" style="color:#517fa4;height:40px;line-height:40px;font-size:16px;">
                  
                 </i>
                </a>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:8px;border-left-width:7px;border-right-width:7px;border-color:white transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483647;top:30px;left:50%;margin-left:-7px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                </div>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:9px;border-left-width:8px;border-right-width:8px;border-color:#e7e7e7 transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483646;top:29px;left:50%;margin-left:-8px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                </div>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="position:absolute;overflow:hidden;margin-top:-3px;margin-left:-71.5px;top:40px;left:50%;right:;display:inline-block;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                 <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">
                  <div style="width:133px;height:20px;">
                   <div class="instagram-follow-button" style="width:133px;height:20px;">
                    <a class="view-on-instagram" href="http://instagram.com/yahootravel?ref=badge" target="_blank">
                     <span class="Hidden">
                      View on Instagram
                     </span>
                    </a>
                   </div>
                  </div>
                 </div>

               </div>
              </div>
              <div class="Pos-r D-ib Cur-d Va-t" style="height:40px;">
               <div class="D-ib" style="height:40px;padding:0 11.5px;">
                <a class="D-ib" href="https://www.pinterest.com/yahootravel" rel="me" target="_blank">
                 <i class="Icon Fw-n Va-t" style="color:#cc2127;height:40px;line-height:40px;font-size:16px;">
                  
                 </i>
                </a>
                <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:8px;border-left-width:7px;border-right-width:7px;border-color:white transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483647;top:30px;left:50%;margin-left:-7px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">

                </div>

                 <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">
                  <div style="width:60px;height:20px;">

          <div class="Pos-r Z-0 article-container legacy" data-template="desktop" id="article-world-s-strangest-bridges" style="background-color:white;min-height:315px;">
           <div class="Pos-r sticky-container print-article" style="min-height:315px;">
            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                 <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-world-s-strangest-bridges">
                      World's strangest bridges
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-world-s-strangest-bridges" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t provider-info">
                          <a class="provider-logo" href="http://www.travelandleisure.com/" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="Travel+Leisure" class="Maw-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/v.4xOrSeLQElwvDE7vIwUw--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO2ZpPWZpdDt3PTE1MA--/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/07/23/TL-jpg_220740.jpg"/>
                          </a>
                          <div class="provider-alias C-n">
                           <a class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-b" href="http://www.travelandleisure.com/" target="_blank">
                            Travel+Leisure
                           </a>
                          </div>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            Adam McCulloch
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             November 6, 2012
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-world-s-strangest-bridges" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          Most bridges have a simple mission: to transport people and vehicles from point A to point B efficiently. But where is the fun in that?
                          <br/>
                          <br/>
                          <span class="Apple-style-span" style="color:#000000;font-size:medium;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:normal;letter-spacing:normal;orphans:2;text-transform:none;white-space:normal;widows:2;word-spacing:0px;border-collapse:separate;font-family:helvetica;">
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <div>
                          <h4 style="margin:3px 0px 8px 5px;padding:0px;font-size:10px;font-weight:bold;font-family:verdana;color:#555555;text-transform:uppercase;">
                           MORE AT TRAVEL + LEISURE
                          </h4>
                          <ul style="margin:3px;padding:0px;list-style-type:none;font-family:verdana;font-size:10px;">
                           <li style="margin:0px 0px 6px 3px;padding:0px;list-style-type:none;list-style-position:inside;">
                            <em style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;color:#db612d;">
                             
                            </em>
                            <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                            </span>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.travelandleisure.com/articles/americas-worst-airports-for-flight-delays" style="color:#1053fc;text-decoration:none;" target="_blank">
                             Americas Worst Airports for Flight Delays
                             <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                             </span>
                             <br/>
                            </a>
                           </li>
                           <li style="margin:0px 0px 6px 3px;padding:0px;list-style-type:none;list-style-position:inside;">
                            <em style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;color:#db612d;">
                             
                            </em>
                            <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                            </span>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.travelandleisure.com/articles/funny-signs-from-around-the-world" style="color:#1053fc;text-decoration:none;" target="_blank">
                             Funny Signs From Around the World
                             <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                             </span>
                             <br/>
                            </a>
                           </li>
                           <li style="margin:0px 0px 6px 3px;padding:0px;list-style-type:none;list-style-position:inside;">
                            <em style="font-style:normal;font-weight:normal;color:#db612d;">
                             
                            </em>
                            <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                            </span>
                            <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.travelandleisure.com/articles/americas-best-cities-for-hipsters" style="color:#1053fc;text-decoration:none;" target="_blank">
                             Americas Best Cities for Hipsters
                             <span class="Apple-converted-space">
                             </span>
                             <br/>
                            </a>
                           </li>
                          </ul>
                         </div>
                         <span>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          Some civil engineers and architects have let their imaginations run free when it comes to designing these spans, producing wonderfully strange bridges that confound, amuse, and sometimes solve complex planning challenges.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Take, for example, the Tianjin Eye Bridge in
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501618-china_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           China
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , whose six lanes are straddled by one of the worlds largest Ferris wheels, or the Sunken Bridge in the
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501776-netherlands_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Netherlands
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , which appears to lead pedestrians through rather than over the water.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Check out more of the worlds unusual bridges: we guarantee you wont regret making the crossing.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Tianjin Eye:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-482564-tianjin_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Tianjin, China
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="World's strangest bridges" class="editorial " src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/JLqG2l4ERymQShze4jUxOw--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-tianjin-eye-jpg_202917.jpg" title="(Photo: Imaginechina/Corbis)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: Imaginechina/Corbis)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          When is a bridge not quite a bridge? When its a Ferris wheel, of course. The Tianjin Eye is a 394-foot-tall carnival ride over the Haihe River in northern
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501618-china_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           China
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          . Completed in 2007, the six-lane bridge incorporates 48 passenger capsules, each with a capacity of eight people. One full rotation takes half an hour, creating the perfect diversion for commuters stuck in bridge traffic.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Lego Bridge:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-485075-wuppertal_germany_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Wuppertal, Germany
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/beBuq5JesbR_vAybgr1xbQ--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-lego-bridge-jpg_203300.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: Rolf Dellenbusch)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: Rolf Dellenbusch)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Few bridges can boast a wonderful view from their underside. This apparently ordinary span was transformed over a period of four weeks by a street artist known as Megx into what resembles a supersize
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://yhoo.it/SuIXk9" target="_blank">
                           Lego
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          construction, delivering a bright dose of childhood nostalgia for drivers passing beneath.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Rolling Bridge:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501822-london_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           London
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/Cok7knB4mTI1OiVzOpn4rQ--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-rolling-bridge-jpg_203431.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: Heatherwick Studio)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: Heatherwick Studio)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Architecture firm Heatherwick studio rose to the challenge of designing a bridge to span the narrow Grand Union Canal at Londons Paddington Basinwhile still allowing ships free passage. The strange, ingenious bridge is made of eight identical segments capable of rolling and unrolling like a party noisemaker. Every Friday at midday the hydraulic-powered construction is activated (regardless of boat traffic) to the amusement of waiting pedestrians.
                         </span>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Sunken Bridge: Halsteren,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501776-netherlands_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Netherlands
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/lLmPZSvRLoxVINRrNFFQbQ--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-sunken-bridge-jpg_203941.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: Courtesy of Product Insider)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: Courtesy of Product Insider)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Building a bridge over troubled waters makes sense. Building a bridge through the very waters you are trying to avoid is just plain crazy. Ro Koster and Ad Kil Architects constructed a remarkable sunken bridge in Halsteren to cross the defensive moat at Fort de Roovere, built in the 1700s to protect the Netherlands from invasion by France and Spain.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Falkirk Wheel:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-490374-falkirk_united_kingdom_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Falkirk, Scotland
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/AOeJZrA1zKyBpsPn20SxYw--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-falkirk-wheel-jpg_204127.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: Courtesy of The Falkirk Wheel)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: Courtesy of The Falkirk Wheel)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          A series of 11 locks once raised small ships the 115 feet from the Union Canal to the Forth and Clyde Canal above. When the entire mechanism was disassembled in 1933, this vital shipping link was broken. Seeking to reconnect the two canals, in 2002, British Waterways built the Falkirk Wheel, a strange contraption that allows ships to sail into a sealed bathlike pod that then rotates, bringing the boat to the new water level above.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Slauerhoffbrug: Leeuwarden,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501776-netherlands_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Netherlands
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/8AnRe8.KXSXD.YhINCQKeA--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-slauerhoffbrug-jpg_204405.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: VAN DRIEL MECHATRONICA)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: VAN DRIEL MECHATRONICA)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          In M. C. Eschers hometown of Leeuwarden stands a bridge that resembles something out of War of the Worlds. When a ship traveling down the Harlinger Vaart River needs to cross traffic, a mechanical arm removes a 50-foot square section of road and hoists it aloft like a giant robot flipping a pancake.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Friendship Bridge: Nantan,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501636-japan_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Japan
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/2RjDC2QbLgTkbsj18ZhBSA--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-friendship-bridge-jpg_204602.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: Courtesy of Norihiko Dan and Associates)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: Courtesy of Norihiko Dan and Associates)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Ordinarily, a bridge is the shortest distance between two banks. The Friendship Bridge is no ordinary bridge. Located in the wellness resort town of Yoshi Springs, just outside of
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501639-kyoto_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Kyoto
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , this bridge traces out a circle 262 feet in diameter. It was designed by Japanese architects Norihiko Dan and Associates and is meant to add to the contemplative serenity of the resort.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          London Bridge:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-473938-lake_havasu_city_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Lake Havasu, AZ
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/K1v53XhnDEkSrsbcu2pRiA--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-london-bridge-jpg_204806.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: Michael Dwyer / Alamy)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: Michael Dwyer / Alamy)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          This would be an ordinary bridge if it were still spanning the River Thames in London, England. What makes this century-old construction preposterous is the fact that in 1968 it was bought by chain-saw magnate Robert McCulloch, disassembled stone by stone, then transported to remote Lake Havasu, where it is now a rather incongruous local landmark (along with other oddities like one-third-scale functioning lighthouses).
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Crab Bridge: Christmas Island,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191502041-australia_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Australia
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <div>
                           <img align="right" alt="" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/QQqjY743VcZixRw9GKMEVw--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-crab-bridge-jpg_205009.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: Courtesy of Christmas Island National Park)" width="320"/>
                           <p class="legend">
                            (Photo: Courtesy of Christmas Island National Park)
                           </p>
                          </div>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Why did the crab cross the road? To get to the other sideand join 120 million of his relatives. Christmas Island, a tiny Australian territory 230 miles off the coast of
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-191501631-indonesia_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Indonesia
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          , sees an annual migration of red crabs, journeying from their spawning grounds, located inland, to the ocean. The crabs migrate in such staggering numbers that roads become impassable, leading wildlife rangers to erect some of the strangest (and heavily trafficked bridges) on the planet.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <strong>
                          Henderson Waves Bridge:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://travel.yahoo.com/p-travelguide-488166-singapore_vacations-i" target="_blank">
                           Singapore
                          </a>
                         </strong>
                         <span>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:f661cf9c-2f21-3943-9c02-22d928b99615;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.flickr.com/photos/86979007@N00/" target="_blank">
                           <span class="yui-editorial-embed">
                            <div>
                             <img align="right" alt="(Photo: ABDUL RAHMAN LATIFF / Flickr)" class="editorial " data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/iOlkHNV1O4OrkaXH6tdD_g--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw/https://s.yimg.com/os/153/2012/10/24/201210-w-strangest-bridges-henderson-waves-jpg_205257.jpg" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" title="(Photo: ABDUL RAHMAN LATIFF / Flickr)" width="320"/>
                             <p class="legend">
                              (Photo: ABDUL RAHMAN LATIFF / Flickr)
                             </p>
                            </div>
                           </span>
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          Connecting two bucolic hilltop parks in busy Singapore, this undulating sculpture of steel ribs resembles a Slinky, with dips and valleys concealing seating and vantage points from which to observe Henderson Road, 118 feet below. The pedestrian-only bridge lights up the night sky.
                         </span>
                         <br/>
                         <br/>
                         <span>
                          <a href="http://www.travelandleisure.com/articles/worlds-strangest-bridges/12" target="_blank">
                           See More of the Worlds Strangest Bridges
                          </a>
                         </span>
                         <span>
                          .
                         </span>
                         <p>
                         </p>
                        </div>

                      <a data-action-outcome="open" data-routable-url="/travel/1/daydream-yosemite-national-park-in-california-124019148432.html" data-ylk="g:c1b0fb56-8eba-3cbd-a625-f188fa9d2ac2;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:also;ad:0;cpos:3;itc:0;t8:tileview;t9:21;elm:img;elmt:ct;" href="/travel/daydream-yosemite-national-park-in-california-124019148432.html" style="color:#000;">

Greenlands Finest Microbrew Beers","summary":"I'm a beer woman. So on my trip to Greenland, when I heard there was a craft brewery in town, I made a beeline for it.","body":"\u003Cp\u003EAnybody who knows me knows I don&#x2019;t drink vodka. I don&#x2019;t do tequila. And I&#x2019;ve never been a big fan of anything that comes with a garnish. I am, however, a beer girl. Raised in Cincinnati, a town with German roots, I have a deep love of hops, and over the years my tastes have been refined from \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhudepohlbeer.com\u002F\"\u003EHudepohl\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and Schlitz to craft beers. Don&#x2019;t get me wrong &#x2014; when stuck on a riverboat for a bachelorette party in, say, Austin, Texas (thanks to my sister Emily), I will still happily down a Bud, a Coors, or a Schlitz. But I have learned to appreciate the fine craft of beer making and love a small-batch brew. So on my trip to Greenland, when I heard there was a craft brewery in town, I made a beeline for it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Ffinger-pulling-head-pulling-and-kick-the-seal-122521580652.html\"\u003EFinger Pulling and Kick the Seal &#x2014; Welcome to the Arctic Games!\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F93fb6d09ed4cf36c50b1cd8100b9a9da95be5f9d.png\" alt=\"Taste-Testing Greenland&#x2019;s Finest Microbrew Beers\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Godthaab Bryghus brewery is in a building that conveniently also houses a dive bar called Daddy&#x2019;s. While &#x201C;Daddy&#x201D; is a great guy named Gert, the actual brewery is run by Mikael Sorenson, who swears that the beer there is made with glacier ice that is at least 2,000 years old.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Yes, we have men who go out onto the ice and cut slabs off the glaciers for us and bring them back here for our beer,&#x201D; Sorenson said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E[Side note: Apparently ice cutting is a big business. Down the street is an ice cream shop that also uses 2,000-year-old ice. &#x201C;Ice cream in Greenland?&#x201D; you may be asking. &#x201C;Isn&#x2019;t it cold enough?&#x201D; No. It&#x2019;s not. Greenland has the second largest ice cream consumption per capita in the world, second only to Finland. Go figure.]\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F3a590de53797cb2f646953e3212a190735cb2dff.png\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhile there are no official stats on how much beer is consumed in &#xA0;Nuuk, Greenland&#x2019;s capital, judging by the crowds in the bars and the continual snow, I&#x2019;d say it ranks right up there. And frankly, I can&#x2019;t say I blame them &#x2014; the weather is rough (see previous episode: &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fsnowmageddon-2015-cabin-fever-hits-hard-in-123462240287.html\"\u003ESnowmageddon 2015: Cabin Fever Hits Hard in Greenland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x201D;), and the beer is delicious. At the time I visited, there were five beers on tap, including the Musk Ox, the Eric the Red, and the Polar Bear (they like to name the beers after local animals). And here&#x2019;s a tip: While they are all delicious, if you ever find yourself at Daddy&#x2019;s in Nuuk, ask for Gert and Mikael and get them to give you the unfiltered versions of all the beers. They may smell like dirty feet, but they taste like heaven.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fsnowmageddon-2015-cabin-fever-hits-hard-in-123462240287.html\"\u003ESnowmageddon 2015: Cabin Fever Hits Hard in Greenland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere is only one problem with the Godthaab Bryghus beer &#x2014; while it is possibly the best beer I have ever tasted (and trust: I have tasted a lot of beer), they don&#x2019;t export. So to get 2,000-year-old glacier-water beer, you have to go to the source. It&#x2019;s worth it. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELet Yahoo Travel inspire you every day. The Tianjin Eye is a 394-foot-tall carnival ride over the Haihe River in northern \n\u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-191501618-china_vacations-i\"\u003EChina\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Completed in 2007, the six-lane bridge incorporates 48 passenger capsules, each with a capacity of eight people. One full rotation takes half an hour, creating the perfect diversion for commuters stuck in bridge traffic.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ELego Bridge: \u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-485075-wuppertal_germany_vacations-i\"\u003EWuppertal, Germany\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"(Photo: Rolf Dellenbusch)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"320\" align=\"right\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002FbeBuq5JesbR_vAybgr1xbQ--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F10\u002F24\u002F201210-w-strangest-bridges-lego-bridge-jpg_203300.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003E(Photo: Rolf Dellenbusch)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EFew bridges can boast a wonderful view from their underside. The strange, ingenious bridge is made of eight identical segments capable of rolling and unrolling like a party noisemaker. Every Friday at midday the hydraulic-powered construction is activated (regardless of boat traffic) to the amusement of waiting pedestrians.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ESunken Bridge: Halsteren, \u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-191501776-netherlands_vacations-i\"\u003ENetherlands\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"(Photo: Courtesy of Product Insider)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"320\" align=\"right\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002FlLmPZSvRLoxVINRrNFFQbQ--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F10\u002F24\u002F201210-w-strangest-bridges-sunken-bridge-jpg_203941.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003E(Photo: Courtesy of Product Insider)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EBuilding a bridge over troubled waters makes sense. Building a bridge through the very waters you are trying to avoid is just plain crazy. Ro Koster and Ad Kil Architects constructed a remarkable sunken bridge in Halsteren to cross the defensive moat at Fort de Roovere, built in the 1700s to protect the Netherlands from invasion by France and Spain.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EFalkirk Wheel: \u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-490374-falkirk_united_kingdom_vacations-i\"\u003EFalkirk, Scotland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"(Photo: Courtesy of The Falkirk Wheel)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"320\" align=\"right\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002FAOeJZrA1zKyBpsPn20SxYw--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F10\u002F24\u002F201210-w-strangest-bridges-falkirk-wheel-jpg_204127.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003E(Photo: Courtesy of The Falkirk Wheel)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EA series of 11 locks once raised small ships the 115 feet from the Union Canal to the Forth and Clyde Canal above. When the entire mechanism was disassembled in 1933, this vital shipping link was broken. Seeking to reconnect the two canals, in 2002, British Waterways built the Falkirk Wheel, a strange contraption that allows ships to sail into a sealed bathlike pod that then rotates, bringing the boat to the new water level above.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003ESlauerhoffbrug: Leeuwarden, \u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-191501776-netherlands_vacations-i\"\u003ENetherlands\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"(Photo: VAN DRIEL MECHATRONICA)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"320\" align=\"right\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002F8AnRe8.KXSXD.YhINCQKeA--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F10\u002F24\u002F201210-w-strangest-bridges-slauerhoffbrug-jpg_204405.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003E(Photo: VAN DRIEL MECHATRONICA)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EIn M. C. Escher&#x2019;s hometown of Leeuwarden stands a bridge that resembles something out of War of the Worlds. When a ship traveling down the Harlinger Vaart River needs to cross traffic, a mechanical arm removes a 50-foot square section of road and hoists it aloft like a giant robot flipping a pancake.\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cstrong\u003EFriendship Bridge: Nantan, \u003Ca target=\"_blank\" href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftravel.yahoo.com\u002Fp-travelguide-191501636-japan_vacations-i\"\u003EJapan\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\n\u003Cspan class=\"yui-editorial-embed\"\u003E\u003Cdiv\u003E\u003Cimg title=\"(Photo: Courtesy of Norihiko Dan and Associates)\" alt=\"\" class=\"editorial \" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"320\" align=\"right\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Flo\u002Fapi\u002Fres\u002F1.2\u002F2RjDC2QbLgTkbsj18ZhBSA--\u002FYXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9MzIw\u002Fhttps:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fos\u002F153\u002F2012\u002F10\u002F24\u002F201210-w-strangest-bridges-friendship-bridge-jpg_204602.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cp class=\"legend\"\u003E(Photo: Courtesy of Norihiko Dan and Associates)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003E\n\u003Cbr\u003EOrdinarily, a bridge is the shortest distance between two banks. The Friendship Bridge is no ordinary bridge.
